220 SUBTITLE C. SURPLUS PROPERTY FUND
221 Sec. 1021. Short title.
222 This subtitle may be cited as the “Surplus Property Sales Fund Amendment Act of 2025”.
223 Sec. 1022. Section 805 of the Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective
224 October 22, 2015 (D.C. Law 21-36; D.C. Official Code § 2-358.05), is amended as follows:
225 (a) Subsection (c) is amended to read as follows:
226 “(c) Money in the Fund shall be used to pay the operational costs of OCP.”.
227 (b) Subsection (d) is amended to read as follows:
228 “(d) Any money remaining available in the Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as determined
229 by the Chief Financial Officer in the fiscal year-end close, shall be transferred to the unassigned
230 fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as part of the fiscal year-end
231 close.”.
232 SUBTITLE D. RECREATIONAL FACILITIES ASSESSMENT
233 Sec. 1031. Short title.
12

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
234 This subtitle may be cited as the “Recreational Facilities Assessment Amendment Act of
235 2025”.
236 Sec. 1032. The Department of General Services Establishment Act of 2011, effective
237 September 14, 2011 (D.C. Law 19-21; D.C. Official Code § 10-551.01 et. seq.), is amended by
238 adding a new section 1028i to read as follows:
239 “Sec. 1028i. Recreational facilities assessment.
240 “(a) The Department shall conduct an annual survey to update information on the
241 condition of spray parks, artificial turf fields, playgrounds, and courts such as tennis, pickleball,
242 basketball, or other similar hard surface courts, as determined by the Department, at recreational
243 facilities. The survey results shall be disaggregated by facility, made publicly available, and
244 transmitted to the Council, the Council chairpersons with oversight jurisdiction over the
245 Department and the Department of Parks and Recreation, and the Office of the City
246 Administrator by March 1 of each year.
247 “(b) For the purposes of this section, the term “recreation facility” shall have the same
248 meaning as set forth in section 1028c(2).”.
249 SUBTITLE E. HUMAN SERVICES GRANT ADMINISTRATION
250 Sec. 1041. Short title.
251 This subtitle may be cited as the “Human Services Grant Administration Amendment Act
252 of 2025”.
13

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
253 Sec. 1042. The Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C.
254 Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code § 1-328.11 et seq.), is amended by adding a new section 1099 to
255 read as follows:
256 “Sec. 1099. (a) For grants the grant agreements for which are received by the Department
257 of Human Services (“DHS”) signed by the grantee after October 1, 2025, which are funded
258 exclusively by local operating funds, and for which DHS is the sole grantor (“DHS local
259 grants”), the first payment to the grantee under the grant shall issue no later than 30 days
260 following the start of the fiscal year or other term of service during which the grantee must
261 perform under its grant agreement with DHS or no later than 30 days following the actual receipt
262 by DHS of a signed grant agreement, whichever is later.
263 “(b) DHS shall provide the grant agreement for each DHS local grant to the grantee for
264 the grantee’s review and signature no later than 30 days following the start of the fiscal year or
265 other term of service during which the grantee must perform under its grant agreement with
266 DHS.”.

804 Sec. 2112. The Council finds that:
805 (1) The Truxton Circle neighborhood is a mixed-use neighborhood characterized
806 by mixed-density residential, commercial, and retail uses. It is a high-priority corridor for
807 investment, in-fill development, and the revitalization of vacant and underutilized lots.
808 (2) Lot 48 in Square 3100 (“the Property”), located at approximately 1600 North
809 Capitol Street, NW, is approximately 18,984 square feet, located at the northwest intersection of
810 North Capitol Street, NW, and Florida Avenue, NW. It is bounded by North Capitol Street, NW,
811 to the east, Q Street, NW, to the south, and Florida Avenue, NW, to the west.
812 (3) The property is at the intersection of two major District corridors and
813 development of these areas is a high-priority measure for the District and residents of Ward 5.
814 (4) The property presents the opportunity for redevelopment along North Capitol
815 Street, NW, and a reduction in blight. This parcel is ripe for matter-of-right, neighborhood-
816 appropriate development, including housing, retail, mixed-use development, and office space.
817 (5) Acquisition of the property by the District will allow for development to
818 invigorate a vacant and underutilized parcel and to reposition the property for development and
819 revitalization.

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL

897 “(1) “Historic burial ground” means a cemetery or any natural or prepared
898 physical location, whether originally below, on, or above the surface of the earth, into which
899 human remains are deposited as a part of the death rite or ceremony of a culture, and that was
900 established in the District of Columbia prior to January 1, 1955, for interments of African
901 Americans and is owned by a public body or qualified charitable organization.
902 “(2) “Qualified charitable organization” means a charitable corporation, charitable
903 association, or charitable trust that has been granted tax-exempt status under § 501(c)(3) of the
904 Internal Revenue Code and that has the primary purpose of preserving historical cemeteries and
905 graves or was formed for the purpose of identifying, preserving, or maintaining historic burial
906 grounds.”.

999 Blossom Festival (“Program”), which shall be administered by the Washington Convention and
1000 Sports Authority (“Events DC”). Under the Program, a matching grant shall be awarded to a
1001 nonprofit organization that organizes and produces an event or events as part of the official,
1002 month-long National Cherry Blossom Festival (“Festival”) at a rate of $2 for every dollar that the

1009 awarded by Events DC in support of the Festival.

1011 In Fiscal Year 2026, Events DC shall issue a grant of no less than $350,000 for the

1013 provides education about how the District of Columbia has been the home for the fight for
1014 freedom and democracy, with an emphasis on including the entire District across all 8 wards in

1133 SUBTITLE E. BACKGROUND CHECK AND RAP BACK PROGRAM
61

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
1134 Sec. 3041. Short title.
1135 This subtitle may be cited as the “Background Check Fingerprinting Authority and Rap
1136 Back Program Act of 2025”.
1137 Sec. 3042. Definitions.
1138 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
1139 (1) “Covered individual” means an individual who has submitted to a fingerprint-
1140 based background check as a condition of caring for children, persons with a disability, the
1141 elderly, or vulnerable adults, a security officer, special police officer, private detective, private
1142 detective agency, security agency, or other person responsible for protecting property, preventing
1143 theft, damage to real or personal property, assaults, disorder, or other illegal occurrences, or for
1144 purposes of licensure, appointment, commission, certification, registration, employment, or
1145 volunteer service with a participating agency pursuant to District law or regulation.
1146 (2) “FBI” means the Federal Bureau of Investigation.
1147 (3) “FBI Rap Back Service” means the FBI Next Generation Identification
1148 Record of Arrest and Prosecution Background Service.
1149 (4) “MPD” means the Metropolitan Police Department.
1150 (5) “Notification event” means an event, such as an arrest or other criminal
1151 activity when fingerprints are taken, that triggers a notification from the FBI Rap Back Service to
62

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
1152 the Metropolitan Police Department regarding a covered individual who has been subscribed to
1153 the FBI Rap Back Service.
1154 (6) “Participating agency” means a District government agency that requires a
1155 fingerprint-based background check and receives the results as a condition of caring for children,
1156 persons with a disability, the elderly, vulnerable adults, a security officer, special police officer,
1157 private detective, private detective agency, security agency, or other person responsible for
1158 protecting property, preventing theft, damage to real or personal property, assaults, disorder, or
1159 similar illegal occurrences, or for purposes of licensure, appointment, commission, certification,
1160 registration, employment, or volunteer service.
1161 Sec. 3043. Background check fingerprinting authority.
1162 (a) If the fingerprinting of an individual is required or authorized by any District or
1163 federal law or regulation for the purposes of conducting a background check of the individual,
1164 MPD, or an entity authorized by MPD, may fingerprint the individual, forward the fingerprints to
1165 the FBI for the purpose of conducting a criminal history check, receive the results of the criminal
1166 history check, and disseminate the results of the criminal history check to entities authorized to
1167 receive the results.
1168 (b) The authority provided by this section applies to fingerprinting authorized under the
1169 District of Columbia Rap Back Program and to fingerprinting required or authorized by any
1170 other District or federal law or regulation.
63

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
1171 Sec. 3044. District of Columbia Rap Back Program.
1172 (a) MPD shall participate on behalf of the District in the FBI Rap Back Service, through
1173 the establishment of a District of Columbia Rap Back Program.
1174 (b) The purpose of the District of Columbia Rap Back Program shall be to allow
1175 participating agencies, through the District of Columbia Rap Back Program, to subscribe covered
1176 individuals in the FBI Rap Back Service and to be notified when a covered individual is the
1177 subject of an FBI Rap Back Service notification event.
1178 (c) If a participating agency requests that the District of Columbia Rap Back Program
1179 subscribe a covered individual in the FBI Rap Back Service, the covered individual shall be
1180 fingerprinted by MPD or an entity authorized by MPD and the fingerprints shall be forwarded by
1181 MPD to the FBI for a national criminal history check and subscription in the FBI Rap Back
1182 Service.
1183 (d) MPD shall notify the relevant participating agency when a covered individual
1184 subscribed by the participating agency in the FBI Rap Back Service through the District of
1185 Columbia Rap Back Program is the subject of an FBI Rap Back Service notification event.
1186 (e) For the purposes of administering the District of Columbia Rap Back Program and
1187 performing or facilitating criminal history background screenings, MPD is authorized to take the
1188 fingerprints of a covered individual, submit to the FBI the fingerprints of, and accompanying
64

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
1189 records regarding, a covered individual, and allow such fingerprints and records to be retained by
1190 the FBI Rap Back Service and used for ongoing searches through the FBI Rap Back Service.
1191 Sec. 3045. Limitation on use of information.
1192 The information contained in a notification event received by a participating agency shall
1193 be used by the participating agency only for the purpose of determining a covered individual’s
1194 eligibility to care for children, persons with a disability, the elderly, or vulnerable adults, a
1195 security officer, special police officer, private detective, private detective agency, security
1196 agency, or other person responsible for protecting property, preventing theft, damage to real or
1197 personal property, assaults, disorders, or similar illegal occurrences, or for purposes of licensure,
1198 appointment, commission, certification, registration, employment, or volunteer service and shall
1199 not be further disseminated by the participating agency.
1200 Sec. 3046. Fees.
1201 MPD may establish by rule a fee, to be imposed on a covered individual or participating
1202 agency, for subscription of a covered individual in the District of Columbia Rap Back
1203 Program. The fee may be imposed on an annual basis.
1204 Sec. 3047. Rules.
1205 MPD may issue rules, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative
1206 Procedure Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), to
65

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
1207 govern the implementation of the District of Columbia Rap Back Program and to otherwise
1208 implement the provisions of this subtitle.

1608 feasibility study for the development and operation of a new dual-language education program or
1609 dual-language education school, located in Ward 6, 7, or 8 and serving grades 6 through 8.
1610 “(b) The study shall:
1611 “(1) Consider the feasibility of:
1612 “(A) Using the Winston Education Campus as a site for a dual-language
1613 education program or a school that hosts a dual-language education program;
1614 “(B) Embedding a dual-language education program into an existing
1615 middle school in Ward 6, 7, or 8, including Kelly Miller Middle School, Kramer Middle School,
1616 Sousa Middle School, and Jefferson Academy Middle School;
1617 “(C) Utilizing the Shirley Chisholm Elementary School modernization to
1618 establish a dual-language education campus at Shirley Chisholm Elementary School; and
96

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
1619 “(D) Incorporating Ward 6, 7, and 8 dual-language education public
1620 charter school elementary schools without an existing or nearby middle school feeder into a
1621 DCPS dual-language education program or middle school feeder pattern;
1622 “(2) Assess the feasibility of each option in paragraph (1) of this subsection based
1623 on the following considerations:
1624 “(A) Capital and operational costs;
1625 “(B) Staffing requirements and models;
1626 “(C) The transportation time of the students and families likely to attend
1627 the new school or program;
1628 “(D) The impact on enrollment patterns of the elementary and middle
1629 schools in the proposed or existing feeder patterns; and
1630 “(E) Enrollment trends of English learners, by in-boundary and out-of-
1631 boundary status, to attend such a dual-language program or school;
1632 “(3) Analyze the demand in Wards 7 and 8 for a dual-language education middle-
1633 grade option, which shall include:

1635 language elementary school in the District outside of those wards; and

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL

1640 language education program or school located in Ward 6, 7, or 8, serving grades 6 through 8.

3429 Fund of the District of Columbia at the end of a fiscal year, or at any other time.

3431 appropriated in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall be continually available without
3432 regard to fiscal year limitation.
3433 (g) For the purposes of this section, the term “RFK campus” means the parcels of land
3434 that are the subject of the Transfer of Jurisdiction Plat recorded in the Surveyor’s Office of the
3435 District of Columbia on February 5, 2025, on page 13 of subdivision book 223, together with any
3436 public streets within or adjacent to such parcels that may be closed from time to time.

4719 systems.”.

4803 “(2) This reporting may be included in the quarterly report required by section
4804 450A(d) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved November 22, 2000 (114 Stat.
4805 2440; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.50a(d)).”.
4806 (b) Section 47-4701(a) is amended to read as follows:

4808 tax abatement financial analysis (“TAFA”) for a permanent bill that grants an exemption or
4809 abatement of a tax imposed by this title or by § 42-1103, unless the exemption or abatement is
4810 one of general applicability.”.

4850 TITLE IX. APPLICABILITY; FISCAL IMPACT; EFFECTIVE DATE
276

ENGROSSED ORIGINAL
4851 Sec. 9001. Applicability.
4852 Except as otherwise provided, this act shall apply as of October 1, 2025.
4853 Sec. 9002. Fiscal impact statement.
4854 The Council adopts the fiscal impact statement of the Chief Financial Officer as the fiscal
4855 impact statement required by section 4a of the General Legislative Procedures Act of 1975,
4856 approved October 16, 2006 (120 Stat. 2038; D.C. Official Code § 1-301.47a).
4857 Sec. 9003. Effective date.
4858 This act shall take effect following approval by the Mayor (or in the event of veto by the
4859 Mayor, action by the Council to override the veto), a 60-day period of congressional review as
4860 provided in section 602(c)(2) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved December
4861 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 813; D.C. Official Code § 1-206.02(c)(2)), and publication in the District of
4862 Columbia Register.
